Letâ€™s Build and Train our Model!

#creating pandas series

data = pd.read_csv('open_ave_data.csv')
exname = data['ExamName']
clin =data['clinicaldata'].dropna()
find=data['findings']
imp =data['impression']
#creating sentences lists for each section

stopwords_list=stopwords.words('english')

exname_sentences = []
for w in exname:
    w=w.lower()
    w=re.sub(r'[^\w\s]','',w)
    w=re.sub(r"([0-9])", r" ",w)
    words = w.split() 
    clean_words = [word for word in words if (word not in stopwords_list) and len(word) > 2]
    exname_sentences.append(" ".join(clean_words))

clin_sentences = []
for w in clin:
    w=w.lower()
    w=re.sub(r'[^\w\s]','',w)
    w=re.sub(r"([0-9])", r" ",w)
    words = w.split() 
    clean_words = [word for word in words if (word not in stopwords_list) and len(word) > 2]
    clin_sentences.append(" ".join(clean_words))

find_sentences = []
for w in find:
    w=w.lower()
    w=re.sub(r'[^\w\s]','',w)
    w=re.sub(r"([0-9])", r" ",w)
    words = w.split() 
    clean_words = [word for word in words if (word not in stopwords_list) and len(word) > 2]
    find_sentences.append(" ".join(clean_words))

imp_sentences = []
for w in imp:
    w=w.lower()
    w=re.sub(r'[^\w\s]','',w)
    w=re.sub(r"([0-9])", r" ",w)
    words = w.split() 
    clean_words = [word for word in words if (word not in stopwords_list) and len(word) > 2]
    imp_sentences.append(" ".join(clean_words))
#Splitting Sentences by Words

def split_sentences(sentences):
    split_sentences = []
    for sentence in sentences:
        split_sentences.append(sentence.split())
    return split_sentences


exname=split_sentences(exname_sentences)
clin=split_sentences(clin_sentences)
find=split_sentences(find_sentences)
imp=split_sentences(imp_sentences)
all_sentences= exname+clin+find+imp
#Let's create and train the model

cores= multiprocessing.cpu_count()
model = Word2Vec(min_count=5,window=5,vector_size=300,workers=cores-1,max_vocab_size=100000)
model.build_vocab(exname)
len(model.wv)
49
model.build_vocab(clin,update=True)
len(model.wv)
106
model.build_vocab(find,update=True)
len(model.wv)
327
model.build_vocab(imp,update=True)

Using the trained model

Exam Name is largely similar, shown by its clustering. Clinical data has a few small clusters, demonstrating that there are a few main types of clinical histories that are sending patients to pursue radiology services. Findings produced the most vocabulary words, shown by the large number of red points. Its spread also demonstrates the large variation in the words used in this section.

In comparison with tf-idf vectorization, the spread looks similar, although the amount of points are reduced due to the size of the word2vec vector being smaller than the tf-idf vector.

Logistic Regression

y = np.empty(X.shape[0])
y[0:49] = 0
y[49:106] = 1
y[106:327] = 2
y[327:X.shape[0]] = 3

X.shape, y.shape
((357, 300), (357,))
#Splitting our dataset into training and testing sets

X_train, X_test, y_train, y_test = train_test_split(
    X,y, test_size=.33, shuffle=True, random_state=52
)
#Logistic Regression

lr_model = LogisticRegression(max_iter=10000)
param_dict = {'C': [0.001, 0.01, 0.1, 1, 10, 100],
             'solver': ['liblinear','sag', 'lbfgs', 'saga']}

start = time()
grid_search = GridSearchCV(lr_model, param_dict)
grid_search.fit(X_train, y_train)
print("GridSearch took %.2f seconds to complete." % (time()-start))
display(grid_search.best_params_)
print("Cross-Validated Score of the Best Estimator: %.3f" % grid_search.best_score_)

lr=LogisticRegression(C=.1, solver ='liblinear')
lr.fit(X_train, y_train)
lr_preds=lr.predict(X_test)

print(confusion_matrix(y_test, lr_preds))
print(classification_report(y_test, lr_preds))
print("Accuracy Score: %.3f" % accuracy_score(y_test, lr_preds))

This model is less accurate than the one based on tf-idf vectorization. One limitation of word2vec is that the library is optimized for analyzing word embeddings more so than sentence embeddings. To further explore sentences, I will use TensorFlow and Googleâ€™s Universal Sentence Encoder to explore classification that way.

# Load the Universal Sentence Encoder's TF Hub module

module_url = "https://tfhub.dev/google/universal-sentence-encoder/4" #@param ["https://tfhub.dev/google/universal-sentence-encoder/4", "https://tfhub.dev/google/universal-sentence-encoder-large/5"]
model = hub.load(module_url)
print ("module %s loaded" % module_url)
def embed(input):
  return model(input)
module https://tfhub.dev/google/universal-sentence-encoder/4 loaded
# One of the advantages of Universal Sentence Encoder is that sentences do not need to be modified as much.

exname0 = data['ExamName']
clin0 =data['clinicaldata'].dropna()
find0=data['findings']
imp0 =data['impression']
exname0_sentences = []
for w in exname0:
    exname0_sentences.append(w)

clin0_sentences = []
for w in clin0:
    clin0_sentences.append(w)

find0_sentences = []
for w in find0:
    find0_sentences.append(w)

imp0_sentences = []
for w in imp0:
    imp0_sentences.append(w)

len(exname0_sentences),len(clin0_sentences),len(find0_sentences),len(imp0_sentences)
(954, 950, 954, 954)
#merging the lists

sentences_list = []

my_lists = [exname0_sentences,clin0_sentences,find0_sentences,imp0_sentences]

for v in my_lists:
    for i in v:
        sentences_list.append(i)

len(sentences_list)
3812
sentences_list = tf.convert_to_tensor(sentences_list)
# Reduce logging output.

logging.set_verbosity(logging.ERROR)

messages=sentences_list

message_embeddings = embed(messages)

for i, message_embedding in enumerate(np.array(message_embeddings).tolist()):
  print("Message: {}".format(messages[i]))
  print("Embedding size: {}".format(len(message_embedding)))
  message_embedding_snippet = ", ".join(
      (str(x) for x in message_embedding[:3]))
  print("Embedding: [{}, ...]\n".format(message_embedding_snippet))

y[1904:2858] = 2
y[2858:X.shape[0]] = 3

#Splitting our dataset into training and testing sets

X_train, X_test, y_train, y_test = train_test_split(
    X,y, test_size=.33, shuffle=True, random_state=52
)
#Logistic Regression

lr_model = LogisticRegression(max_iter=2000)
param_dict = {'C': [0.001, 0.01, 0.1, 1, 10,100],
             'solver': ['liblinear','sag', 'lbfgs', 'saga']}
